The Conservatives felt let down by France over the <a href="/wiki/Chanak_Crisis" title="Chanak Crisis">Chanak Crisis</a>, with Bonar Law telling France, "We cannot act alone as the policeman of the world."<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>  The Conservative leader, <a href="/wiki/Austen_Chamberlain" title="Austen Chamberlain">Austen Chamberlain</a>, summoned a <a href="/wiki/Carlton_Club_meeting,_19_October_1922" class="mw-redirect" title="Carlton Club meeting, 19 October 1922">meeting of Conservative Members of Parliament</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Carlton_Club" title="Carlton Club">Carlton Club</a> to discuss their attitude to the Coalition in the forthcoming election. Chamberlain and most Conservative leaders supported Lloyd George; however, the rank and file rejected the coalition. The main attack came from <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Baldwin" title="Stanley Baldwin">Stanley Baldwin</a>, then President of the Board of Trade, who spoke of Lloyd George as a "dynamic force" who would break the Conservative Party. They sealed Lloyd George's fate on 19 October 1922 by voting in favour of the motion to end the coalition and fight the election "as an independent party, with its own leader and its own programme." Lloyd George submitted his resignation to the King that afternoon.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Later_political_career_.281922.E2.80.931945.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Later_political_career_(1922–1945)">Later political career (1922–1945)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Lloyd_George&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Later political career (1922–1945)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Liberal_reunion">Liberal reunion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Lloyd_George&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Liberal reunion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:David_Lloyd_George_-_Project_Gutenberg_eText_15306.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/David_Lloyd_George_-_Project_Gutenberg_eText_15306.jpg/170px-David_Lloyd_George_-_Project_Gutenberg_eText_15306.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="237" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/David_Lloyd_George_-_Project_Gutenberg_eText_15306.jpg/255px-David_Lloyd_George_-_Project_Gutenberg_eText_15306.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/David_Lloyd_George_-_Project_Gutenberg_eText_15306.jpg/340px-David_Lloyd_George_-_Project_Gutenberg_eText_15306.jpg 2x" data-file-width="503" data-file-height="700" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:David_Lloyd_George_-_Project_Gutenberg_eText_15306.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>David Lloyd George</div></div></div>
<p>Throughout the 1920s Lloyd George remained highly visible in politics; predictions that he would return to power were common, but it never happened.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> He still controlled a large fund (thought to have been between £1m and £3m, or £50m–£150m at 2015 prices) from his investments in newspaper ownership and from his sale of titles.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Before the <a href="/wiki/1923_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="1923 United Kingdom general election">1923 election</a>, he resolved his dispute with Asquith, allowing the Liberals to run a united ticket against <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Baldwin" title="Stanley Baldwin">Stanley Baldwin</a>'s policy of protective tariffs. Baldwin both feared and despised Lloyd George, and one of his aims was to keep him out of power. He later claimed that he had adopted tariffs, which cost the Conservatives their majority, out of concern that Lloyd George was about to do so on his return from a tour of North America. Although there was press speculation at the time that Lloyd George would do so (or adopt <a href="/wiki/US-style_Prohibition" class="mw-redirect" title="US-style Prohibition">US-style Prohibition</a> to appeal to <a href="/wiki/Representation_of_the_People_Act_1918" title="Representation of the People Act 1918">newly enfranchised</a> women voters), there is no evidence that this was his intent.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> Asquith and Lloyd George reached agreement on 13 November 1923 and issued a joint Free Trade manifesto, followed by a more general one. Lloyd George agreed to contribute £100,000 (in the event he claimed to have contributed £160,000 including help given to individual candidates; Liberal HQ put the number at £90,000).<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1924 Lloyd George, realising that Liberal defeat was inevitable and keen to take control of the party himself, spent only £60,000.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/1924_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="1924 United Kingdom general election">1924 general election</a>, Baldwin won a clear victory, the leading coalitionists such as Austen Chamberlain and Lord Birkenhead (and former Liberal <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a>) agreeing to serve under Baldwin and thus ruling out any restoration of the 1916–22 coalition.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Liberal_leader">Liberal leader</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Lloyd_George&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Liberal leader">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vera_%26_Chaim_Weizmann,_Herbert_Samuel,_Lloyd_George,_Ethel_Snowden,_Philip_Snowden.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Vera_%26_Chaim_Weizmann%2C_Herbert_Samuel%2C_Lloyd_George%2C_Ethel_Snowden%2C_Philip_Snowden.jpeg/230px-Vera_%26_Chaim_Weizmann%2C_Herbert_Samuel%2C_Lloyd_George%2C_Ethel_Snowden%2C_Philip_Snowden.jpeg" decoding="async" width="230" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Vera_%26_Chaim_Weizmann%2C_Herbert_Samuel%2C_Lloyd_George%2C_Ethel_Snowden%2C_Philip_Snowden.jpeg/345px-Vera_%26_Chaim_Weizmann%2C_Herbert_Samuel%2C_Lloyd_George%2C_Ethel_Snowden%2C_Philip_Snowden.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Vera_%26_Chaim_Weizmann%2C_Herbert_Samuel%2C_Lloyd_George%2C_Ethel_Snowden%2C_Philip_Snowden.jpeg/460px-Vera_%26_Chaim_Weizmann%2C_Herbert_Samuel%2C_Lloyd_George%2C_Ethel_Snowden%2C_Philip_Snowden.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="2399" data-file-height="1746" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vera_%26_Chaim_Weizmann,_Herbert_Samuel,_Lloyd_George,_Ethel_Snowden,_Philip_Snowden.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Vera_Weizmann" title="Vera Weizmann">Vera Weizmann</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chaim_Weizmann" title="Chaim Weizmann">Chaim Weizmann</a>, <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Samuel" class="mw-redirect" title="Herbert Samuel">Herbert Samuel</a>, Lloyd George, <a href="/wiki/Ethel_Snowden" title="Ethel Snowden">Ethel Snowden</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Philip_Snowden" class="mw-redirect" title="Philip Snowden">Philip Snowden</a></div></div></div><p>The disastrous election result in 1924 left the Liberals as a weak third party in British politics, with just over 40 MPs. Although Asquith, who had again lost his seat and was created an <a href="/wiki/Earl_of_Oxford_and_Asquith" title="Earl of Oxford and Asquith">Earl</a>, remained Liberal leader, Lloyd George was elected chairman of the Liberal MPs by 26 votes to 7. <a href="/wiki/John_Simon,_1st_Viscount_Simon" title="John Simon, 1st Viscount Simon">Sir John Simon</a> and his followers were still loyal to Asquith (after 1931 Simon would lead a breakaway <a href="/wiki/National_Liberal_Party_(UK,_1931)" title="National Liberal Party (UK, 1931)">National Liberal Party</a>, which eventually merged with the Conservatives) whilst <a href="/wiki/Walter_Runciman,_1st_Viscount_Runciman_of_Doxford" title="Walter Runciman, 1st Viscount Runciman of Doxford">Walter Runciman</a> led a separate radical group within the Parliamentary Party.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lloyd George was now mainly interested in the reform of land ownership, but had only been permitted to put a brief paragraph about it in the hastily drafted 1924 Liberal manifesto. In the autumn of 1925, despite the hostility of <a href="/wiki/Charles_Hobhouse" title="Charles Hobhouse">Charles Hobhouse</a>, Runciman and <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Mond,_1st_Baron_Melchett" title="Alfred Mond, 1st Baron Melchett">Alfred Mond</a>, he began an independent campaign, soon to become “The Land and the Nation” (the "Green Book", first of a series of policy pamphlets produced by Lloyd George in the late 1920s). Asquith rebuked him, but was ignored, and they reached an agreement in principle on 2 December, then together they presented Lloyd George's plans to the <a href="/wiki/National_Liberal_Federation" title="National Liberal Federation">National Liberal Federation</a> on 26 February 1926.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Liberal Shadow Cabinet, including Lloyd George, unequivocally backed Baldwin's handling of the <a href="/wiki/1926_United_Kingdom_general_strike" title="1926 United Kingdom general strike">General Strike</a> on 3 May, but Lloyd George then wrote an article for the American press more sympathetic to the strikers, and did not attend the Shadow Cabinet on 10 May, sending his apologies on “policy grounds”. Asquith sent him a public letter (20 May) rebuking him for not attending the meeting to discuss his opinions with colleagues in private. Lloyd George's letter of 10 May had not been published, making it appear that Asquith had fired the first shot, and Lloyd George sent a public reply, moderate in tone (the journalist <a href="/wiki/C._P._Scott" title="C. P. Scott">C. P. Scott</a> helped him draft it), on 25 May. In late May, the executive of the National Liberal Federation convened to plan the agenda for the following month's conference. 16 were pro Asquith and 8 pro Lloyd George; they planned a motion expressing confidence in Asquith, but another option was also proposed to seek Asquith's opinion first, and also general feeling of regret at having been forced to choose between Asquith and Lloyd George. Asquith then wrote another public letter (1 June) stating that he regarded Lloyd George's behaviour as tantamount to resignation, the same as if a Cabinet Minister had refused to abide by the principle of collective responsibility. Twelve leading Liberals wrote in Asquith's support to <i>“The Times”</i> (1 June); however, Lloyd George had more support in the wider party than among the grandees: the London Liberal Candidates’ Association (3 June) defied its officers and expressed its dismay at the split, effectively supporting Lloyd George, and on 8 June the Liberal MPs voted 20:10 urging a reconciliation. Asquith had planned to launch a fightback at the National Liberal Federation in Weston-Super-Mare, but on 12 June, five days before the conference was due to start, he suffered a stroke which put him out of action for three months. Lloyd George was given a rapturous welcome. Asquith resigned as party leader in October, dying in 1928.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As Liberal leader at last, Lloyd George used his fund to finance candidates and put forward innovative ideas for public works to reduce unemployment (as detailed in pamphlets such as the "<a href="/wiki/Britain%27s_Industrial_Future" title="Britain&#39;s Industrial Future">Yellow Book</a>" and the "Orange Book"). <a href="/wiki/Charles_Masterman" title="Charles Masterman">Charles Masterman</a> later wrote: "When Lloyd George came back to the party, ideas came back to the party".<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> Lloyd George was also helped by <a href="/wiki/John_Maynard_Keynes" title="John Maynard Keynes">John Maynard Keynes</a> to write <i>We can Conquer Unemployment</i>, setting out economic policies to solve unemployment. In 1927 Lloyd George gave £300,000 plus an annual grant of between £30,000 and £40,000 for the operations of the Liberal headquarters. He also gave £2,000 per annum to the parliamentary party until 1931.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> Even with the money the results at the <a href="/wiki/1929_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="1929 United Kingdom general election">1929 general election</a> were disappointing. The Liberals increased their support only to 60 or so seats, while Labour became the largest party for the first time. Once again, the Liberals ended up supporting a minority Labour government. In 1929 Lloyd George became <a href="/wiki/Father_of_the_House" title="Father of the House">Father of the House</a> (longest-serving member of the Commons), an honorific position without power.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marginalised">Marginalised</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Lloyd_George&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Marginalised">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1931 an illness prevented his joining the <a href="/wiki/UK_National_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="UK National Government">National Government</a> when it was formed. Later when the National Government called a General Election he tried to pull the Liberal Party out of it but succeeded in taking only a few followers, most of whom were related to him; the main Liberal Party remained in the coalition for a year longer, under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Samuel,_1st_Viscount_Samuel" title="Herbert Samuel, 1st Viscount Samuel">Sir Herbert Samuel</a>. By the 1930s Lloyd George was on the margins of British politics, although still intermittently in the public eye and publishing his <i>War Memoirs</i>. Lloyd George was President of the London Welsh Trust, which runs the <a href="/wiki/London_Welsh_Centre" title="London Welsh Centre">London Welsh Centre</a>, Gray's Inn Road, from 1934 until 1935.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Lloyd_George.27s_.22New_Deal.22"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Lloyd_George's_&quot;New_Deal&quot;">Lloyd George's "New Deal"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Lloyd_George&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Lloyd George&#039;s &quot;New Deal&quot;">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LloydGeorgeEn1932.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/LloydGeorgeEn1932.jpeg/220px-LloydGeorgeEn1932.jpeg" decoding="async" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/LloydGeorgeEn1932.jpeg/330px-LloydGeorgeEn1932.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/LloydGeorgeEn1932.jpeg/440px-LloydGeorgeEn1932.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="679" data-file-height="542" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LloydGeorgeEn1932.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lloyd George in 1932</div></div></div>
<p>In January 1935 Lloyd George announced a programme of economic reform, called "Lloyd George's New Deal" after the American <a href="/wiki/New_Deal" title="New Deal">New Deal</a>. This <a href="/wiki/John_Maynard_Keynes" title="John Maynard Keynes">Keynesian</a> economic programme was essentially the same as that of 1929. MacDonald requested that he put his case before the Cabinet, and so in March Lloyd George submitted a 100-page memorandum that was cross-examined between April and June in ten meetings of the Cabinet's sub-committee; however, the programme did not find favour; two-thirds of Conservative MPs were against Lloyd George's joining the National government, and some Cabinet members would have resigned if he had joined.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Appeasement_of_Germany">Appeasement of Germany</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Lloyd_George&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Appeasement of Germany">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Lloyd George was consistently pro-German after 1923.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> He supported German demands for territorial concessions and recognition of its "great power" status; he paid much less attention to the security concerns of France, Poland, <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovakia</a> and Belgium.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> In a speech in 1933 he warned that if <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a> were overthrown Communism would replace him in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> In August 1934 (following <a href="/wiki/Austrofascism" title="Austrofascism">Austria's transition to fascism</a>), he insisted Germany could not wage war, and assured European nations that there would be no risk of war during the next ten years.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> In September 1936, he went to Germany to talk with Hitler. Hitler said he was pleased to have met "the man who won the war"; Lloyd George was moved, and called Hitler "the greatest living German".<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> Lloyd George also visited Germany's public works programmes and was impressed. On his return to Britain, he wrote an article for the <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Express" title="Daily Express">Daily Express</a></i> praising Hitler, stating: "The Germans have definitely made up their minds never to quarrel with us again."<sup id="cite_ref-Jones_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jones-197">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> He believed Hitler was "the George Washington of Germany"; that he was rearming Germany for defence and not for offensive war; that a war between Germany and the Soviet Union would not happen for at least ten years; that Hitler admired the British and wanted their friendship but that there was no British leadership to exploit this; however, by 1937, Lloyd George's distaste for <a href="/wiki/Neville_Chamberlain" title="Neville Chamberlain">Neville Chamberlain</a> led him to disavow Chamberlain's appeasement policies.<sup id="cite_ref-Jones_197-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jones-197">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Final_years">Final years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Lloyd_George&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Final years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the last important parliamentary intervention of his career, which occurred during the crucial <a href="/wiki/Norway_Debate" title="Norway Debate">Norway Debate</a> of May 1940, Lloyd George made a powerful speech that helped to undermine Chamberlain as Prime Minister and to pave the way for the ascendancy of Churchill. Churchill offered Lloyd George the agriculture portfolio in his Cabinet but he refused, citing his unwillingness to sit alongside Chamberlain. Lloyd George also thought that Britain's chances in the war were dim, and he remarked to his secretary: "I shall wait until Winston is bust."<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> He wrote to the <a href="/wiki/Hastings_Russell,_12th_Duke_of_Bedford" title="Hastings Russell, 12th Duke of Bedford">Duke of Bedford</a> in September 1940, during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Britain" title="Battle of Britain">Battle of Britain</a>, advocating a negotiated peace with Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A pessimistic speech by Lloyd George on 7 May 1941 led Churchill to compare him with <a href="/wiki/Philippe_P%C3%A9tain" title="Philippe Pétain">Philippe Pétain</a>. On 11 June 1942, he made his last speech in the House of Commons, and he cast his last vote in the Commons on 18 February 1943 as one of the 121 MPs (97 Labour) condemning the Government for its failure to back the <a href="/wiki/Beveridge_Report" title="Beveridge Report">Beveridge Report</a>. Fittingly, his final vote was in defence of the welfare state which he had helped to create.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Although he had displayed political courage all his life, in his last years he gave way to physical timidity and hypochondria.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> He continued to attend Castle Street Baptist Chapel in London, and to preside over the <a href="/wiki/National_Eisteddfod_of_Wales" title="National Eisteddfod of Wales">National Eisteddfod</a> at its Thursday session each summer. In September 1944, he and Frances left his home, <a href="/wiki/Bron-y-de" title="Bron-y-de">Bron-y-de</a> in <a href="/wiki/Churt" title="Churt">Churt</a>, for <a href="/wiki/T%C5%B7_Newydd" title="Tŷ Newydd">Tŷ Newydd</a>, a farm near his boyhood home in Llanystumdwy. He was now weakening rapidly and his voice failing. He was still an MP but had learned that wartime changes in the constituency meant that Carnarvon Boroughs might go Conservative at the next election<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>. On <a href="/wiki/New_Years_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="New Years Day">New Years Day</a> 1945, Lloyd George was raised to the <a href="/wiki/Peerage" title="Peerage">peerage</a> as <a href="/wiki/Earl_Lloyd-George_of_Dwyfor" title="Earl Lloyd-George of Dwyfor">Earl Lloyd-George of Dwyfor</a>, and Viscount Gwynedd, of Dwyfor in the <a href="/wiki/Historic_counties_of_Wales" title="Historic counties of Wales">County</a> of <a href="/wiki/Caernarvonshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Caernarvonshire">Caernarvonshire</a>; however, he did not live long enough to take his seat in the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lords" title="House of Lords">House of Lords</a>  <sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Death">Death</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Lloyd_George&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Death">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bedd_David_Lloyd_George_Llanystumdwy_David_Lloyd_George%27s_Grave_-_geograph.org.uk_-_469205.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Bedd_David_Lloyd_George_Llanystumdwy_David_Lloyd_George%27s_Grave_-_geograph.org.uk_-_469205.jpg/200px-Bedd_David_Lloyd_George_Llanystumdwy_David_Lloyd_George%27s_Grave_-_geograph.org.uk_-_469205.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Bedd_David_Lloyd_George_Llanystumdwy_David_Lloyd_George%27s_Grave_-_geograph.org.uk_-_469205.jpg/300px-Bedd_David_Lloyd_George_Llanystumdwy_David_Lloyd_George%27s_Grave_-_geograph.org.uk_-_469205.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Bedd_David_Lloyd_George_Llanystumdwy_David_Lloyd_George%27s_Grave_-_geograph.org.uk_-_469205.jpg/400px-Bedd_David_Lloyd_George_Llanystumdwy_David_Lloyd_George%27s_Grave_-_geograph.org.uk_-_469205.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="428" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bedd_David_Lloyd_George_Llanystumdwy_David_Lloyd_George%27s_Grave_-_geograph.org.uk_-_469205.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lloyd George's grave, Llanystumdwy</div></div></div>
<p>Lloyd George died of <a href="/wiki/Cancer" title="Cancer">cancer</a> at the age of 82 on 26 March 1945, with his wife Frances and his daughter Megan at his bedside. Four days later, on <a href="/wiki/Good_Friday" title="Good Friday">Good Friday</a>, he was buried beside the <a href="/wiki/Afon_Dwyfor" title="Afon Dwyfor">river Dwyfor</a> in <a href="/wiki/Llanystumdwy" title="Llanystumdwy">Llanystumdwy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> A boulder marks the grave; there is no inscription; however a monument designed by the architect Sir <a href="/wiki/Clough_Williams-Ellis" title="Clough Williams-Ellis">Clough Williams-Ellis</a> was subsequently erected around the grave,<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> bearing an <a href="/wiki/Englyn" title="Englyn">englyn</a> (strict-metre stanza) engraved on slate in his memory composed by his nephew Dr <a href="/wiki/W._R._P._George" title="W. R. P. George">W. R. P. George</a>. Nearby stands the <a href="/wiki/Lloyd_George_Museum" title="Lloyd George Museum">Lloyd George Museum</a>, also designed by Williams-Ellis and opened in 1963.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Assessment">Assessment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Lloyd_George&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Assessment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2><p>
Historian <a href="/wiki/Martin_Pugh_(author)" class="mw-redirect" title="Martin Pugh (author)">Martin Pugh</a> in <i>The Oxford Companion to British History</i> argues that he:</p><blockquote><p>made a greater impact on British public life than any other 20th-cent. statesman. He laid the foundations of what later became the welfare state, and put a progressive income tax system at the centre of government finance. He also left his mark on the system of government by enlarging the scope of the prime minister's role. He was acclaimed, not without reason, as the 'Man Who Won the War'....he was blamed by many Liberals for destroying their party in 1918, hated in the Labour movement for his handling of industrial issues after 1918, and disparaged by Conservatives for his radicalism.<sup id="cite_ref-Martin_Pugh_2002_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Martin_Pugh_2002-205">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p><a href="/wiki/George_Riddell,_1st_Baron_Riddell" title="George Riddell, 1st Baron Riddell">George Riddell, 1st Baron Riddell</a>, a wealthy newspaper publisher, was a close confidant and financial supporter of Lloyd George from 1908 to 1922, and Riddell's revealing diary is a valuable source for the period.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> During Lloyd George's first year as prime minister, in summer 1917, Riddell assessed his personality:</p><blockquote><p>His energy, capacity for work, and power of recuperation are remarkable. He has an extraordinary memory, imagination, and the art of getting at the root of a matter....He is not afraid of responsibility, and has no respect for tradition or convention. He is always ready to examine, scrap or revise established theories and practices.  These qualities give him unlimited confidence in himself.... He is one of the craftiest of men, and his extraordinary charm of manner not only wins him friends, but does much to soften the asperities of his opponents and enemies. He is full of humour and a born actor....He has an instinctive power of divining the thoughts and intentions of people with whom he is conversing...His chief defects are: (1) Lack of appreciation of existing institutions, organisations, and stolid, dull people...their ways are not his ways and their methods are not his methods. (2) Fondness for a grandiose scheme in preference to an attempt to improve existing machinery. (3) Disregard of difficulties in carrying out big projects...he is not a man of detail.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote><p>
Historian John Shepherd wrote in <i><a href="/wiki/History_Today" title="History Today">History Today</a></i>:</p><blockquote>
<p>In any poll of modern historians Winston Churchill and David Lloyd George would emerge as the two most renowned prime ministers during the past century.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
</blockquote>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Family">Family</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Lloyd_George&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Family">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Margaret_and_children">Margaret and children</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Lloyd_George&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Margaret and children">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:TNA_COPY1-560-129_David_and_Megan_Lloyd_George.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/TNA_COPY1-560-129_David_and_Megan_Lloyd_George.jpg/220px-TNA_COPY1-560-129_David_and_Megan_Lloyd_George.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="340" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/TNA_COPY1-560-129_David_and_Megan_Lloyd_George.jpg/330px-TNA_COPY1-560-129_David_and_Megan_Lloyd_George.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/TNA_COPY1-560-129_David_and_Megan_Lloyd_George.jpg/440px-TNA_COPY1-560-129_David_and_Megan_Lloyd_George.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="926" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:TNA_COPY1-560-129_David_and_Megan_Lloyd_George.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>David Lloyd George with his daughter Megan in 1911</div></div></div>
<p>He had five children by his first wife, Margaret: Richard (1889–1968), Mair (1890–1907, who died during an <a href="/wiki/Appendectomy" title="Appendectomy">appendectomy</a>), Olwen (1892–1990), Gwilym (1894–1967) and Megan (1902–1966). He remained married to Margaret, and remained fond of her until her death<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> on 20 January 1941; Lloyd George was deeply upset by the fact that bad weather prevented him from being with her when she died.
</p><p>His son, <a href="/wiki/Gwilym_Lloyd_George,_1st_Viscount_Tenby" class="mw-redirect" title="Gwilym Lloyd George, 1st Viscount Tenby">Gwilym</a>, and his daughter, <a href="/wiki/Megan_Lloyd_George" title="Megan Lloyd George">Megan</a>, both followed him into politics, and were elected members of parliament. They were politically faithful to their father throughout his life, but after 1945 each drifted away from the Liberal Party, Gwilym finishing his career as a Conservative <a href="/wiki/Home_Secretary" title="Home Secretary">Home Secretary</a> and Megan becoming a Labour MP in 1957.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Frances">Frances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Lloyd_George&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Frances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In October 1943, aged 80, and to the disapproval of his children,<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> he married his secretary and mistress, <a href="/wiki/Frances_Lloyd_George" class="mw-redirect" title="Frances Lloyd George">Frances Stevenson</a>. He had first met Stevenson in 1910, and she had worked for him first as a teacher for Megan in 1911;<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> their affair began in early 1913.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> Lloyd George may well have been the father of Stevenson's daughter Jennifer (1929–2012), born long before they wed.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Frances was the first Countess Lloyd-George, and is now largely remembered for her diaries, which dealt with the great issues, and statesmen, of Lloyd George's heyday. A volume of their letters, <i>My Darling Pussy</i>, has also been published; Lloyd George's nickname for Frances referred to her gentle personality.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Descendants">Descendants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Lloyd_George&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Descendants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Canadian historian <a href="/wiki/Margaret_MacMillan" title="Margaret MacMillan">Margaret MacMillan</a>, who detailed Lloyd George's role at the 1919 Peace Conference in her book, <i><a href="/wiki/Peacemakers:_The_Paris_Peace_Conference_of_1919_and_Its_Attempt_to_End_War" title="Peacemakers: The Paris Peace Conference of 1919 and Its Attempt to End War">Peacemakers</a></i>, is his great-granddaughter. The British television historian and presenter <a href="/wiki/Dan_Snow" title="Dan Snow">Dan Snow</a> is a great-great-grandson.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> Other descendants include the late <a href="/wiki/Owen_Lloyd_George,_3rd_Earl_Lloyd-George_of_Dwyfor" title="Owen Lloyd George, 3rd Earl Lloyd-George of Dwyfor">Owen, 3rd Earl Lloyd-George</a>, his grandson, and the late 3rd Earl's younger son The Hon. Robert Lloyd George (Chairman of Lloyd George Management),<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> brother of David, the 4th and present Earl, who has two sons: Viscount Gwynedd (born 1986), a journalist, and Captain the Hon. Fred Lloyd George, an officer in the Welsh Guards (born 1987).
</p>
<h2><span id="Lloyd_George.27s_Cabinets"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Lloyd_George's_Cabinets">Lloyd George's Cabinets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Lloyd_George&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Lloyd George&#039;s Cabinets">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=David_Lloyd_George&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="War_Cabinet">War Cabinet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Lloyd_George&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: War Cabinet">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/George_Nathaniel_Curzon,_1st_Marquess_Curzon_of_Kedleston" class="mw-redirect" title="George Nathaniel Curzon, 1st Marquess Curzon of Kedleston">Lord Curzon of Kedleston</a> – <a href="/wiki/Lord_President_of_the_Council" title="Lord President of the Council">Lord President of the Council</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leader_of_the_House_of_Lords" title="Leader of the House of Lords">Leader of the House of Lords</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bonar_Law" title="Bonar Law">Bonar Law</a> – <a href="/wiki/Chancellor_of_the_Exchequer" title="Chancellor of the Exchequer">Chancellor of the Exchequer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leader_of_the_House_of_Commons" title="Leader of the House of Commons">Leader of the House of Commons</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Arthur_Henderson" title="Arthur Henderson">Arthur Henderson</a> – <a href="/wiki/Minister_without_Portfolio" class="mw-redirect" title="Minister without Portfolio">Minister without Portfolio</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alfred_Milner,_1st_Viscount_Milner" title="Alfred Milner, 1st Viscount Milner">Lord Milner</a> – Minister without Portfolio</li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="War_Cabinet_changes">War Cabinet changes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Lloyd_George&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: War Cabinet changes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li>May–August 1917 – In temporary absence of Arthur Henderson, <a href="/wiki/George_Barnes_(British_politician)" title="George Barnes (British politician)">George Barnes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_Pensions_(Britain)" class="mw-redirect" title="Minister of Pensions (Britain)">Minister of Pensions</a>, acts as a member of the War Cabinet.</li>
<li>June 1917 – <a href="/wiki/Jan_Smuts" title="Jan Smuts">Jan Smuts</a> enters the War Cabinet as a Minister without Portfolio</li>
<li>July 1917 – <a href="/wiki/Edward_Carson" title="Edward Carson">Sir Edward Carson</a> enters the War Cabinet as a Minister without Portfolio</li>
<li>August 1917 – George Barnes succeeds Arthur Henderson (resigned) as Minister without Portfolio and <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour Party</a> member of the War Cabinet.</li>
<li>January 1918 – Carson resigns and is not replaced</li>
<li>April 1918 – <a href="/wiki/Austen_Chamberlain" title="Austen Chamberlain">Austen Chamberlain</a> succeeds Lord Milner as Minister without Portfolio.</li>
<li>January 1919 Law becomes <a href="/wiki/Lord_Privy_Seal" title="Lord Privy Seal">Lord Privy Seal</a>, remaining Leader of the House of Commons, and is succeeded as Chancellor of the Exchequer by Chamberlain; both remaining in the War Cabinet. Smuts is succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Eric_Geddes" title="Eric Geddes">Sir Eric Geddes</a> as <a href="/wiki/Minister_without_Portfolio" class="mw-redirect" title="Minister without Portfolio">Minister without Portfolio</a>.</li></ul>
<h4><span id="Other_members_of_Lloyd_George.27s_War_Government"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_members_of_Lloyd_George's_War_Government">Other members of Lloyd George's War Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Lloyd_George&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: Other members of Lloyd George&#039;s War Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Robert_Finlay,_1st_Viscount_Finlay" title="Robert Finlay, 1st Viscount Finlay">Lord Finlay</a> – <a href="/wiki/Lord_Chancellor" title="Lord Chancellor">Lord Chancellor</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/David_Lindsay,_27th_Earl_of_Crawford" title="David Lindsay, 27th Earl of Crawford">Lord Crawford</a> – <a href="/wiki/Lord_Privy_Seal" title="Lord Privy Seal">Lord Privy Seal</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/George_Cave,_Viscount_Cave" class="mw-redirect" title="George Cave, Viscount Cave">Sir George Cave</a> – <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_the_Home_Department" class="mw-redirect" title="Secretary of State for the Home Department">Secretary of State for the Home Department</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Arthur_Balfour" title="Arthur Balfour">Arthur Balfour</a> – <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Foreign_Affairs" class="mw-redirect" title="Secretary of State for Foreign Affairs">Secretary of State for Foreign Affairs</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Walter_Long,_1st_Viscount_Long" title="Walter Long, 1st Viscount Long">Walter Long</a> – <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_the_Colonies" title="Secretary of State for the Colonies">Secretary of State for the Colonies</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Edward_Stanley,_17th_Earl_of_Derby" title="Edward Stanley, 17th Earl of Derby">Lord Derby</a>, and then (after April 1918), Lord Milner – <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_War" title="Secretary of State for War">Secretary of State for War</a></li>
<li>Austen Chamberlain (to 1917), and then <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Montagu" title="Edwin Montagu">Edwin Montagu</a> – <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_India" title="Secretary of State for India">Secretary of State for India</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Edward_Carson" title="Edward Carson">Sir Edward Carson</a>, and then (from 1917) <a href="/wiki/Eric_Geddes" title="Eric Geddes">Sir Eric Geddes</a> – <a href="/wiki/First_Lord_of_the_Admiralty" title="First Lord of the Admiralty">First Lord of the Admiralty</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Frederick_Cawley" class="mw-redirect" title="Frederick Cawley">Sir Frederick Cawley</a> (to 1918), and then <a href="/wiki/William_Maxwell_Aitken,_1st_Baron_Beaverbrook" class="mw-redirect" title="William Maxwell Aitken, 1st Baron Beaverbrook">Lord Beaverbrook</a> and <a href="/wiki/William_Fisher,_1st_Baron_Downham" class="mw-redirect" title="William Fisher, 1st Baron Downham">Lord Downham</a> – <a href="/wiki/Chancellor_of_the_Duchy_of_Lancaster" title="Chancellor of the Duchy of Lancaster">Chancellor of the Duchy of Lancaster</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Albert_Stanley,_1st_Baron_Ashfield" title="Albert Stanley, 1st Baron Ashfield">Sir Albert Stanley</a> – <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Board_of_Trade" title="President of the Board of Trade">President of the Board of Trade</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Henry_Duke,_1st_Baron_Merrivale" title="Henry Duke, 1st Baron Merrivale">H. E. Duke</a> and then <a href="/wiki/Edward_Shortt" title="Edward Shortt">Edward Shortt</a> – <a href="/wiki/Chief_Secretary_for_Ireland" title="Chief Secretary for Ireland">Chief Secretary for Ireland</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/William_Fisher,_1st_Baron_Downham" class="mw-redirect" title="William Fisher, 1st Baron Downham">Hayes Fisher</a> – President of the Local Government Board (to 1918)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Auckland_Geddes" class="mw-redirect" title="Auckland Geddes">Sir Auckland Geddes</a> – President of the Local Government Board (to 1919)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a> – Minister of Munitions (appointed 17/7/17)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Neville_Chamberlain" title="Neville Chamberlain">Neville Chamberlain</a>, and then (from 1917) <a href="/wiki/Auckland_Geddes" class="mw-redirect" title="Auckland Geddes">Sir Auckland Geddes</a> – <a href="/wiki/Director_of_National_Service" title="Director of National Service">Director of National Service</a></li></ul>
<h3><span id="Peacetime_Government.2C_January_1919_.E2.80.93_October_1922"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Peacetime_Government,_January_1919_–_October_1922">Peacetime Government, January 1919 – October 1922</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Lloyd_George&amp;action=edit&amp;section=59" title="Edit section: Peacetime Government, January 1919 – October 1922">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The War Cabinet was formally maintained for much of 1919, but as Lloyd George was out of the country for many months this made little difference. In October 1919 a formal Cabinet was reinstated.
</p>
<ul><li>David Lloyd George — Prime Minister</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Frederick_Edwin_Smith,_1st_Earl_of_Birkenhead" class="mw-redirect" title="Frederick Edwin Smith, 1st Earl of Birkenhead">Lord Birkenhead</a> – <a href="/wiki/Lord_Chancellor" title="Lord Chancellor">Lord Chancellor</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/George_Curzon,_1st_Marquess_Curzon_of_Kedleston" title="George Curzon, 1st Marquess Curzon of Kedleston">Lord Curzon of Kedleston</a> – <a href="/wiki/Lord_President_of_the_Council" title="Lord President of the Council">Lord President of the Council</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leader_of_the_House_of_Lords" title="Leader of the House of Lords">Leader of the House of Lords</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bonar_Law" title="Bonar Law">Bonar Law</a> – <a href="/wiki/Lord_Privy_Seal" title="Lord Privy Seal">Lord Privy Seal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leader_of_the_House_of_Commons" title="Leader of the House of Commons">Leader of the House of Commons</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Austen_Chamberlain" title="Austen Chamberlain">Austen Chamberlain</a> – <a href="/wiki/Chancellor_of_the_Exchequer" title="Chancellor of the Exchequer">Chancellor of the Exchequer</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Edward_Shortt" title="Edward Shortt">Edward Shortt</a> – <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_the_Home_Department" class="mw-redirect" title="Secretary of State for the Home Department">Secretary of State for the Home Department</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Arthur_Balfour" title="Arthur Balfour">Arthur Balfour</a> – <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Foreign_Affairs" class="mw-redirect" title="Secretary of State for Foreign Affairs">Secretary of State for Foreign Affairs</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alfred_Milner,_1st_Viscount_Milner" title="Alfred Milner, 1st Viscount Milner">Lord Milner</a> – <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_the_Colonies" title="Secretary of State for the Colonies">Secretary of State for the Colonies</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a> – <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_War" title="Secretary of State for War">Secretary of State for War</a> and <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Air" title="Secretary of State for Air">Air</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Edwin_Montagu" title="Edwin Montagu">Edwin Montagu</a> – <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_India" title="Secretary of State for India">Secretary of State for India</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Walter_Long,_1st_Viscount_Long" title="Walter Long, 1st Viscount Long">Walter Long</a> – <a href="/wiki/First_Lord_of_the_Admiralty" title="First Lord of the Admiralty">First Lord of the Admiralty</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Albert_Stanley,_1st_Baron_Ashfield" title="Albert Stanley, 1st Baron Ashfield">Sir Albert Stanley</a> – <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Board_of_Trade" title="President of the Board of Trade">President of the Board of Trade</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Robert_Munro,_1st_Baron_Alness" title="Robert Munro, 1st Baron Alness">Robert Munro</a> – <a href="/wiki/Secretary_for_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="Secretary for Scotland">Secretary for Scotland</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/James_Ian_Macpherson" class="mw-redirect" title="James Ian Macpherson">Ian Macpherson</a> – <a href="/wiki/Chief_Secretary_for_Ireland" title="Chief Secretary for Ireland">Chief Secretary for Ireland</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/John_French,_1st_Earl_of_Ypres" title="John French, 1st Earl of Ypres">Lord French</a> – <a href="/wiki/Lord-Lieutenant_of_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord-Lieutenant of Ireland">Lord-Lieutenant of Ireland</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Christopher_Addison,_1st_Viscount_Addison" title="Christopher Addison, 1st Viscount Addison">Christopher Addison</a> – <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Local_Government_Board" title="President of the Local Government Board">President of the Local Government Board</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rowland_Prothero" class="mw-redirect" title="Rowland Prothero">Rowland Prothero</a> – <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Board_of_Agriculture" class="mw-redirect" title="President of the Board of Agriculture">President of the Board of Agriculture</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/H._A._L._Fisher" title="H. A. L. Fisher">H. A. L. Fisher</a> – <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Board_of_Education" class="mw-redirect" title="President of the Board of Education">President of the Board of Education</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Andrew_Weir,_1st_Baron_Inverforth" title="Andrew Weir, 1st Baron Inverforth">Lord Inverforth</a> – <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_Munitions" title="Minister of Munitions">Minister of Munitions</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Robert_Stevenson_Horne,_1st_Viscount_Horne" class="mw-redirect" title="Robert Stevenson Horne, 1st Viscount Horne">Sir Robert Horne</a> – <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Employment" title="Secretary of State for Employment">Minister of Labour</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/George_Barnes_(British_politician)" title="George Barnes (British politician)">George Barnes</a> – <a href="/wiki/Minister_without_Portfolio" class="mw-redirect" title="Minister without Portfolio">Minister without Portfolio</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Eric_Geddes" title="Eric Geddes">Sir Eric Geddes</a> – <a href="/wiki/Minister_without_Portfolio" class="mw-redirect" title="Minister without Portfolio">Minister without Portfolio</a></li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Peacetime_changes">Peacetime changes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Lloyd_George&amp;action=edit&amp;section=60" title="Edit section: Peacetime changes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li>May 1919 – Sir Auckland Geddes succeeds Sir Albert Stanley as President of the Board of Trade. Sir Eric Geddes becomes Minister of Transport.</li>
<li>October 1919 – Lord Curzon of Kedleston succeeds Balfour as Foreign Secretary. Balfour succeeds Curzon as Lord President. The Local Government Board is abolished. Christopher Addison becomes Minister of Health. The Board of Agriculture is abolished. <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Lee,_1st_Viscount_Lee_of_Fareham" title="Arthur Lee, 1st Viscount Lee of Fareham">Lord Lee of Fareham</a> becomes Minister of Agriculture. Sir Eric Geddes becomes Minister of Transport.</li>
<li>January 1920 – George Barnes leaves the cabinet.</li>
<li>March 1920 – Sir Robert Horne succeeds Sir Auckland Geddes as President of the Board of Trade. <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Macnamara" title="Thomas Macnamara">Thomas Macnamara</a> succeeds Horne as Minister of Labour.</li>
<li>April 1920 – Sir <a href="/wiki/Hamar_Greenwood" class="mw-redirect" title="Hamar Greenwood">Hamar Greenwood</a> succeeds Ian Macpherson as Chief Secretary for Ireland. Sir <a href="/wiki/Laming_Worthington-Evans" title="Laming Worthington-Evans">Laming Worthington-Evans</a> joins the Cabinet as Minister without Portfolio.</li>
<li>February 1921 – Winston Churchill succeeds Lord Milner as Colonial Secretary. Sir Laming Worthington-Evans succeeds Churchill as War Secretary. <a href="/wiki/Freddie_Guest" title="Freddie Guest">Freddie Guest</a>, Churchill's successor as Air Secretary, was not in the Cabinet. Lord Lee of Fareham succeeds Walter Long at the Admiralty. <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Griffith-Boscawen" title="Arthur Griffith-Boscawen">Sir Arthur Griffith-Boscawen</a> succeeds Lee as Minister of Agriculture.</li>
<li>March 1921 – Austen Chamberlain succeeds Bonar Law as Lord Privy Seal and Leader of the Commons. Sir Robert Horne succeeds Chamberlain at the Exchequer. Stanley Baldwin succeeds Horne at the Board of Trade.</li>
<li>April 1921 – Lord French resigns from the cabinet, remaining Lord Lieutenant of Ireland. Christopher Addison becomes a Minister without Portfolio. Sir Alfred Mond succeeds him as Minister of Health. The Ministry of Munitions is abolished.</li>
<li>November 1921 – Sir Eric Geddes resigns from the cabinet. His successor as Minister of Transport, <a href="/wiki/William_Peel,_1st_Earl_Peel" title="William Peel, 1st Earl Peel">Viscount Peel</a>, is not in the Cabinet. The Attorney General, Sir <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Hewart" class="mw-redirect" title="Gordon Hewart">Gordon Hewart</a>, enters the Cabinet.</li>
<li>March 1922 – Lord Peel succeeds Edwin Montagu as India Secretary.</li>
<li>April 1922 – The <a href="/wiki/First_Commissioner_of_Works" title="First Commissioner of Works">First Commissioner of Works</a>, Lord Crawford, enters the Cabinet.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Styles_of_address_and_honours">Styles of address and honours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Lloyd_George&amp;action=edit&amp;section=61" title="Edit section: Styles of address and honours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:132px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Earl_Lloyd_George_of_Dwyfor_arms.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Earl_Lloyd_George_of_Dwyfor_arms.svg/130px-Earl_Lloyd_George_of_Dwyfor_arms.svg.png" decoding="async" width="130" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Earl_Lloyd_George_of_Dwyfor_arms.svg/195px-Earl_Lloyd_George_of_Dwyfor_arms.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Earl_Lloyd_George_of_Dwyfor_arms.svg/260px-Earl_Lloyd_George_of_Dwyfor_arms.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="570" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Earl_Lloyd_George_of_Dwyfor_arms.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Lloyd George <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms" title="Coat of arms">arms</a></i></div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Styles_of_address">Styles of address</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Lloyd_George&amp;action=edit&amp;section=62" title="Edit section: Styles of address">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>1863–1890: Mr David Lloyd George</li>
<li>1890–1906: Mr David Lloyd George MP</li>
<li>1906–1919: <i>The Rt Hon</i> David Lloyd George MP</li>
<li>1919–1945: <i>The Rt Hon</i> David Lloyd George OM MP</li>
<li>1945: <i>The Rt Hon</i> The Earl Lloyd-George of Dwyfor OM PC</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Peerage">Peerage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Lloyd_George&amp;action=edit&amp;section=63" title="Edit section: Peerage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/File:Coronet_of_a_British_Earl.svg" class="image"><img alt="Coronet of a British Earl.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Coronet_of_a_British_Earl.svg/30px-Coronet_of_a_British_Earl.svg.png" decoding="async" width="30" height="23" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Coronet_of_a_British_Earl.svg/45px-Coronet_of_a_British_Earl.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Coronet_of_a_British_Earl.svg/60px-Coronet_of_a_British_Earl.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="256" data-file-height="199" /></a> <b>Earl Lloyd-George of Dwyfor</b>, <i><b>Viscount Gwynedd</b></i>, of Dwyfor in the county of Caernarvonshire (created 12 February 1945).</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Decorations">Decorations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Lloyd_George&amp;action=edit&amp;section=64" title="Edit section: Decorations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/File:Order_of_Merit_(Commonwealth_realms)_ribbon.png" class="image"><img alt="Order of Merit (Commonwealth realms) ribbon.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Order_of_Merit_%28Commonwealth_realms%29_ribbon.png/60px-Order_of_Merit_%28Commonwealth_realms%29_ribbon.png" decoding="async" width="60" height="18" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Order_of_Merit_%28Commonwealth_realms%29_ribbon.png/90px-Order_of_Merit_%28Commonwealth_realms%29_ribbon.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/3a/Order_of_Merit_%28Commonwealth_realms%29_ribbon.png 2x" data-file-width="100" data-file-height="30" /></a> <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Merit" title="Order of Merit">Order of Merit</a> (Civil) 1919<sup id="cite_ref-WhoLloydGeorge_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WhoLloydGeorge-217">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/File:Order_of_St_John_(UK)_ribbon.png" class="image"><img alt="Order of St John (UK) ribbon.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Order_of_St_John_%28UK%29_ribbon.png/60px-Order_of_St_John_%28UK%29_ribbon.png" decoding="async" width="60" height="18" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Order_of_St_John_%28UK%29_ribbon.png/90px-Order_of_St_John_%28UK%29_ribbon.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/20/Order_of_St_John_%28UK%29_ribbon.png 2x" data-file-width="100" data-file-height="30" /></a> Knight of Grace, <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Saint_John_(chartered_1888)" title="Order of Saint John (chartered 1888)">Order of Saint John</a>; Chancellor of the Welsh Priory from 1918 and Prior of Wales from 1943.<sup id="cite_ref-bpeerage_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bpeerage-21">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/File:Legion_Honneur_GC_ribbon.svg" class="image"><img alt="Legion Honneur GC ribbon.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Legion_Honneur_GC_ribbon.svg/60px-Legion_Honneur_GC_ribbon.svg.png" decoding="async" width="60" height="17" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Legion_Honneur_GC_ribbon.svg/90px-Legion_Honneur_GC_ribbon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Legion_Honneur_GC_ribbon.svg/120px-Legion_Honneur_GC_ribbon.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="218" data-file-height="60" /></a> Grand Cordon of the <a href="/wiki/Legion_of_Honour" title="Legion of Honour">Legion of Honour</a> (France) 1920<sup id="cite_ref-WhoLloydGeorge_217-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WhoLloydGeorge-217">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/File:Grand_Crest_Ordre_de_Leopold.png" class="image"><img alt="Grand Crest Ordre de Leopold.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Grand_Crest_Ordre_de_Leopold.png/60px-Grand_Crest_Ordre_de_Leopold.png" decoding="async" width="60" height="17" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Grand_Crest_Ordre_de_Leopold.png/90px-Grand_Crest_Ordre_de_Leopold.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Grand_Crest_Ordre_de_Leopold.png/120px-Grand_Crest_Ordre_de_Leopold.png 2x" data-file-width="218" data-file-height="60" /></a> Grand Cordon of the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Leopold_(Belgium)" title="Order of Leopold (Belgium)">Order of Leopold (Belgium)</a><sup id="cite_ref-kellys_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kellys-20">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/File:Cavaliere_di_gran_Croce_Regno_SSML_BAR.svg" class="image"><img alt="Cavaliere di gran Croce Regno SSML BAR.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Cavaliere_di_gran_Croce_Regno_SSML_BAR.svg/60px-Cavaliere_di_gran_Croce_Regno_SSML_BAR.svg.png" decoding="async" width="60" height="17" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Cavaliere_di_gran_Croce_Regno_SSML_BAR.svg/90px-Cavaliere_di_gran_Croce_Regno_SSML_BAR.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Cavaliere_di_gran_Croce_Regno_SSML_BAR.svg/120px-Cavaliere_di_gran_Croce_Regno_SSML_BAR.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="218" data-file-height="60" /></a> Grand Cross of the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_St_Maurice_and_St_Lazarus" class="mw-redirect" title="Order of St Maurice and St Lazarus">Order of St Maurice and St Lazarus</a> (Italy)<sup id="cite_ref-bpeerage_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bpeerage-21">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/File:EST_Cross_of_Liberty_Civilian_Service.png" class="image"><img alt="EST Cross of Liberty Civilian Service.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/EST_Cross_of_Liberty_Civilian_Service.png/60px-EST_Cross_of_Liberty_Civilian_Service.png" decoding="async" width="60" height="18" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/EST_Cross_of_Liberty_Civilian_Service.png/90px-EST_Cross_of_Liberty_Civilian_Service.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/EST_Cross_of_Liberty_Civilian_Service.png/120px-EST_Cross_of_Liberty_Civilian_Service.png 2x" data-file-width="200" data-file-height="60" /></a> <a href="/wiki/Cross_of_Liberty_(Estonia)" title="Cross of Liberty (Estonia)">Cross of Liberty (Estonia)</a> (3rd class 1st rank) for civilian service, 29 April 1925<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Academic">Academic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Lloyd_George&amp;action=edit&amp;section=65" title="Edit section: Academic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Oxford_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Oxford University">Oxford University</a> – <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Civil_Law" title="Doctor of Civil Law">DCL</a> 1908<sup id="cite_ref-WhoLloydGeorge_217-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WhoLloydGeorge-217">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Fellow" title="Fellow">Fellow</a> of <a href="/wiki/Jesus_College,_Oxford" title="Jesus College, Oxford">Jesus College</a> 1910</li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Wales" title="University of Wales">University of Wales</a> – <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Laws" class="mw-redirect" title="Doctor of Laws">LLD</a> 1908<sup id="cite_ref-WhoLloydGeorge_217-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WhoLloydGeorge-217">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Glasgow_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Glasgow University">Glasgow University</a> – LLD 1917<sup id="cite_ref-bpeerage_21-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bpeerage-21">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Edinburgh" title="University of Edinburgh">University of Edinburgh</a> – LLD 1918<sup id="cite_ref-WhoLloydGeorge_217-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WhoLloydGeorge-217">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Rector_of_the_University_of_Edinburgh" title="Rector of the University of Edinburgh">Rector</a> – 1920<sup id="cite_ref-bpeerage_21-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bpeerage-21">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup></li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Durham_University" title="Durham University">Durham University</a> – DCL 1919<sup id="cite_ref-bpeerage_21-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bpeerage-21">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sheffield_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield University">Sheffield University</a> – <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Letters" title="Doctor of Letters">DLitt</a> 1919<sup id="cite_ref-WhoLloydGeorge_217-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WhoLloydGeorge-217">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cambridge_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Cambridge University">Cambridge University</a> – LLD 1920<sup id="cite_ref-bpeerage_21-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bpeerage-21">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Birmingham_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Birmingham University">Birmingham University</a> – LLD 1921<sup id="cite_ref-bpeerage_21-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bpeerage-21">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Leeds_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Leeds University">Leeds University</a> – LLD 1922<sup id="cite_ref-bpeerage_21-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bpeerage-21">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Freedoms">Freedoms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Lloyd_George&amp;action=edit&amp;section=66" title="Edit section: Freedoms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Lloyd George was made <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_the_City" title="Freedom of the City">Honorary Freeman</a> of the following <a href="/wiki/City" title="City">cities</a> and <a href="/wiki/Town" title="Town">towns</a>:<sup id="cite_ref-bpeerage_21-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bpeerage-21">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Blackpool" title="Blackpool">Blackpool</a><sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup>  – 1918</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/City_of_London" title="City of London">City of London</a>, <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cardiff" title="Cardiff">Cardiff</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bristol" title="Bristol">Bristol</a>, <a href="/wiki/York" title="York">York</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barnsley" title="Barnsley">Barnsley</a> – 1921</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aberystwyth" title="Aberystwyth">Aberystwyth</a> – 1922</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>; <a href="/wiki/Brecon" title="Brecon">Brecon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Llandovery" title="Llandovery">Llandovery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carmarthen" title="Carmarthen">Carmarthen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Llanelli" title="Llanelli">Llanelli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swansea" title="Swansea">Swansea</a> – 1923
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Livery_company#governance" title="Livery company">Master</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Worshipful_Company_of_Curriers" title="Worshipful Company of Curriers">Worshipful Company of Curriers</a> (London)</li></ul></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Namesakes">Namesakes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Lloyd_George&amp;action=edit&amp;section=67" title="Edit section: Namesakes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Lloyd_George_Avenue" title="Lloyd George Avenue">Lloyd George Avenue</a> is an extension of the <a href="/wiki/A470" class="mw-redirect" title="A470">A470</a> road, connecting Central <a href="/wiki/Cardiff" title="Cardiff">Cardiff</a> to <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_Bay" title="Cardiff Bay">Cardiff Bay</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Mount_Lloyd_George" title="Mount Lloyd George">Mount Lloyd George</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Rocky_Mountains" title="Northern Rocky Mountains">Northern Rocky Mountains</a> of <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">British Columbia</a>, Canada was named after Lloyd George during the First World War, and still retains the name.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Kibbutz" title="Kibbutz">Kibbutz</a> <a href="/wiki/Ramat_David" title="Ramat David">Ramat David</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Jezreel_Valley" title="Jezreel Valley">Jezreel Valley</a> in northern <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> and the adjacent <a href="/wiki/Ramat_David_Airbase" title="Ramat David Airbase">Ramat David Airbase</a> are named after him.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/David_Lloyd_George_Elementary_School" class="mw-redirect" title="David Lloyd George Elementary School">David Lloyd George Elementary School</a> in <a href="/wiki/Vancouver" title="Vancouver">Vancouver</a> was named after Lloyd George in 1921.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_depictions">Cultural depictions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Lloyd_George&amp;action=edit&amp;section=68" title="Edit section: Cultural depictions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Cultural_depictions_of_British_prime_ministers#David_Lloyd_George" class="mw-redirect" title="Cultural depictions of British prime ministers">Cultural depictions of British prime ministers §&#160;David Lloyd George</a></div>
<p>See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Cultural_depictions_of_David_Lloyd_George" title="Category:Cultural depictions of David Lloyd George">Category:Cultural depictions of David Lloyd George</a>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Selected_works">Selected works</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Lloyd_George&amp;action=edit&amp;section=69" title="Edit section: Selected works">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><i>Better Times</i>, Hodder &amp; Stoughton 1910</li>
<li><i>Through Terror to Triumph</i> (edited by <a href="/wiki/Frances_Stevenson" title="Frances Stevenson">Frances Stevenson</a>), Hodder and Stoughton, 1915</li>
<li><i>The Great Crusade</i> (edited by Frances Stevenson), Hodder and Stoughton, 1918</li>
<li><i>Is It Peace?</i>, Hodder and Stoughton, 1923</li>
<li><i>Where Are We Going?</i>, George H. Doran Company, 1923 (American version of <i>Is It Peace?</i>, same contents but re-arranged)</li>
<li><i>Slings and Arrows</i> (selected and with an introduction by <a href="/wiki/Philip_Guedalla" title="Philip Guedalla">Philip Guedalla</a>), Cassell and Company, Ltd, 1929</li>
<li><i>The Truth About Reparations and War-Debts</i>, William Heinemann Ltd, 1932</li>
<li><i>War Memoirs</i>, 6 volumes, Ivor Nicholson and Watson, 1933 - 1936: re-published in 2 volumes by Odhams Press, 1938</li>
<li><i>Organizing Prosperity</i>, Ivor Nicholson and Watson, 1935</li>
<li><i>The Truth About the Peace Treaties</i> (published in USA as <i>Memoirs of the Peace Conference</i>), 2 volumes, Victor Gollancz Ltd, 1938</li></ul>

</li>
